?
The scientific aspect requires examining the principles of tawhid and creation 'in accordance with what intellects require.' Have you ever critically tested your own belief in these principles using your reason, or have you accepted them passively? If not, what holds you back from this examination?
?
You read that the Prophet's claim has two parts: that God sent him and that his message is from God. Do you live as if both are true? Specifically, are you obeying the one sent and implementing the message, or do you treat them as separate intellectual beliefs?

The Fourth Condition: Safety from Contradiction
Nasafi defines the fourth condition and explains its logical basis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a valid claim of prophethood must be free from internal contradiction and how contradiction reveals the falsity of the claim.

Core Idea
A contradictory claim is self-defeating: it admits its own falsehood.

In this passage, Nasafi explains the fourth logical condition that any claim to prophethood must satisfy: it must be free from contradiction. He provides a rigorous argument showing that if a claimant contradicts himself, he effectively acknowledges the invalidity of his own claim. Let's examine his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation. Focus on the definition of the condition and the logical argument that follows.
Notice that the condition applies to both the claim and its evidence.
2
Understand the logical argument
The author explains why a contradictory claim is invalid: by claiming one of two contradictories, the claimant implicitly witnesses to the falsity of the other. If he claims both, he admits the falsity of each.
This is a concise logical proof that any internal conflict undermines the claim.
3
Reflect on the importance
Consider why coherence is a basic requirement for any serious assertion, especially in matters of prophethood. This condition ensures that the claimant is not self-refuting.
Acknowledge that this principle applies beyond this specific context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرابع سلامة الدعوى والبيئة عن مناقضة ترد عليهما أو على أحدهما، إذ المناقض معترف بنقض ما ادعاه وفساده، إذ هو بادعائه صحة أحد المتناقضين شاهد ببطلان الآخر، فصار بادعائه صحة كل واحد منهما في محل شاهدا بفساد الآخر، فإذًا صار معترفا بفساد الآخر، فإذا صار معترفًا بفساد كل واحد من الأمرين ثم لا شك في كون صحة الدعوى متعلقة بهذه المعاني.
And the fourth [condition] is safety of the claim and the proof from a contradiction that occurs to both of them or to one of them, for the contradictory [person] is acknowledging the invalidation of what he claimed and its corruption, since by his claiming the soundness of one of the two contradictories he is a witness to the falsity of the other, so by his claiming the soundness of each one of them in a position he becomes a witness to the falsity of the other, thus he becomes an acknowledger of the falsity of the other, and if he becomes an acknowledger of the falsity of each one of the two matters, then there is no doubt that the soundness of the claim is dependent upon these meanings.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth condition for the validity of a claim of prophethood: the claim and its evidence must be free from internal contradiction. The author explains that if a claimant contradicts himself, he effectively admits the falsehood of his own claim. The reasoning is that if a person asserts two contradictory statements, his assertion of the truth of one is a testimony to the falsity of the other. Therefore, if he insists on both, he is acknowledging the corruption of each. Thus, a valid claim must be coherent and free from self-contradiction.

Key Terms
سلامة الدعوى
مناقضة
متناقضين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only obvious contradictions matter; minor inconsistencies do not affect the claim.
Correction: The author emphasizes that any internal conflict, whether obvious or subtle, undermines the claim because a contradictory claimant is acknowledging the falsity of his own position.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what does a contradictory claim reveal about the claimant?
A) He is ignorant of the truth.
B) He is acknowledging the falsity of his own claim.
C) He is being dishonest on purpose.
D) He has two different proofs.

Key Takeaway
The fourth condition requires safety from contradiction because a contradictory claim is inherently self-refuting.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of an area in your life where you hold two inconsistent beliefs or your actions contradict your stated values. According to this lesson, what does that contradiction say about the truth of your claim? Will you resolve it today?
?
This passage teaches that a contradictory claim is self-refuting. Is there a belief about your own character or faith that you profess but that your daily life contradicts? What specific step will you take this week to align them?
?
The principle here applies to all truth claims, not just prophethood. Consider a claim you make about your priorities (e.g., 'I put my deen first'). Does your schedule reflect that, or is there a contradiction? What one change can you make to eliminate that contradiction?

The Theoretical Possibility of the Prophet's Claim
Nasafi establishes the rational possibility of the Prophet's claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi establishes the theoretical possibility of the Prophet's claim by showing that its content—tawhid and creation—aligns with rational proofs, unlike false prophets.

Core Idea
The Prophet's claim is possible because its message is rational.

This passage examines the theoretical aspect of the Prophet's claim. Nasafi argues that the content of the Prophet's message—the principles of tawhid and creation—is rational and consistent with established proofs. In contrast, false prophets like Zoroaster and Mani are self-evidently false due to their ignorance of the Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to understand the overall argument.
Notice the heading clarifies the passage's purpose.
2
Identify the two claims and their possibility
The Prophet claimed two things: that Allah sent him, and that the religion he brought is from Allah. Nasafi states both are possible.
The second claim's possibility is examined through two aspects.
3
Understand the theoretical aspect
The theoretical aspect looks at the content of the call: tawhid, beginning and return of creation. This content is rational and matches earlier proofs.
Contrast with Zoroaster and Mani who displayed ignorance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[أولاً: دعوى الرسول وقعت في حيز الإمكان]: ثم إنه عليه السلام ادعى الرسالة من ربه إلى خلقه فبنا أن نتأمل أن هذه المعاني الأربعة هل وجدت أم لا؟ فنقول : أما دعواه فواقعة في حيز الإمكان فإنه ادعى أمرين: أحدهما أن الله تعالى أرسله إلى الخلق ليدعوهم إلى ما ارتضاه دينا لهم، وهذه في حيز الإمكان بل في حيز وجوب القبول لما اقترن به من الأحوال الخمسة التي مر ذكرها. والثاني: أن ما أتى به هو الذي ارتضاه الله تعالى لعباده، وهو ممكن، ومعرفة إمكانها متعلق باستبراء ذلك من وجهين: أحدهما: الوجه الأول العلمي. والثاني: الوجه العملي. فأما الوجه العلمي فبأن ننظر إلى ما يدعو الخلق إليه من أصول التوحيد وأصول بدء الخلق وإعادته، وقد وجد ذلك بحمد الله على ما تقتضيه العقول وتوجيه الدلائل الموجبة للعلم الحقيقي الذي لا يخالطه شك، ولا ريب على ما مر تقرير ذلك في أول الكتاب من حدوث العالم ووحدانية صانعه، وكانت حالته في ذلك مخالفة لحالة زرادشت وماني فإنهما بنفس ما أظهراه من الجهل بالصانع وصفاته أخيرًا كل من سمع دعواهما بكونهما كاذبين، وبما ادعيا من الرسالة وفي نسبتهما ما أورداه من الدين إلى الباري جل وعلا.
[First: The claim of the Messenger occurred within the realm of possibility]: Then he, peace be upon him, claimed the message from his Lord to His creation, so we must consider whether these four meanings exist or not. So we say: As for his claim, it occurs within the realm of possibility, for he claimed two things: One of them is that Allah the Exalted sent him to the creation to call them to what He approved as a religion for them, and this is within the realm of possibility, nay, within the realm of obligatory acceptance due to the five conditions that accompanied it which have been mentioned previously. The second is that what he brought is what Allah the Exalted approved for His servants, and it is possible, and knowledge of its possibility is dependent on examining it from two aspects: one: the first, theoretical aspect; the second: the practical aspect. As for the theoretical aspect, it is that we look at what he calls the creation to from the principles of tawhid and the principles of the beginning of creation and its return, and we find that, praise be to Allah, according to what the intellects require and the direction of proofs that necessitate true knowledge which is not mixed with doubt or uncertainty, as we have already established at the beginning of the book regarding the temporal origin of the world and the oneness of its Maker. And his state in that was contrary to the state of Zoroaster and Mani, for they, by virtue of what they displayed of ignorance of the Maker and His attributes, informed everyone who heard their claim that they were liars, and by what they claimed of the message and in their attributing to the Exalted and Majestic the religion they presented.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage begins the examination of the Prophet's claim by first asserting its possibility. The author states that the claim involves two things: that Allah sent him, and that the religion he brought is from Allah. Both are possible. The possibility of the religion is known through two aspects: theoretical and practical. The theoretical aspect involves examining the content of his call regarding tawhid, creation, and resurrection, which are found to be rational and consistent with the proofs already established in the beginning of the book about the temporal origin of the world and the oneness of the Creator. In contrast, Zoroaster and Mani displayed ignorance about the Creator and His attributes, so their claims were self-evidently false.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: Possibility of a prophetic claim is merely logical non-contradiction.
Correction: Nasafi shows that possibility includes consistency with established rational truths about tawhid and creation.

A) The miracles he performed
B) The principles of tawhid and creation
C) The practical laws he prescribed
D) The genealogy of the Prophet

Key Takeaway

The Practical Proof of Prophethood
Nasafi defines the practical proof and contrasts with false prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the practical teachings of a prophet serve as evidence for his truthfulness, and how they contrast with false claimants.

Core Idea
The practicality and wisdom of a prophet's teachings reveal their divine origin.

The second proof for a prophet's claim is practical: we examine the content of his teachings. Nasafi argues that the Prophet's prescribed acts of worship and customs are clearly based on sound judgment and reason, unlike the harmful doctrines of Mani and Mazdak. This lesson explores that contrast.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the two main parts: the description of the practical test, and the contrast with Mani and Mazdak.
The passage begins with a heading in brackets indicating this is the second aspect.
2
Understand the practical criterion
Nasafi says we look at the acts of worship and customs the prophet prescribes. They should align with sound judgment and reason. This is the basis for verifying truthfulness.
He promises a later discussion on the wisdom of the Shariah.
3
Contrast with Mani and Mazdak
Mani and Mazdak prohibited beneficial acquisitions and permitted adultery, which harm society. Their teachings contradict wisdom, proving they are false prophets.
This contrast highlights the importance of practical consequences.
4

Consider why the Prophet's teachings promote preservation of life, lineage, and property, while false teachings lead to corruption. This reinforces the truth of Islam.
Think about how this argument applies to other claims.

Commentary

In contrast, Mani and Mazdak taught harmful practices: they prohibited beneficial economic activities and permitted promiscuity, which destroys families and lineages. Thus, their claims are self-evidently false because their teachings contradict wisdom and the common good.

The Practical Evidence for Prophethood
Al-Nasafi presents the practical evidence for prophethood by comparing Islamic law with the harmful laws of Mani and Mazdak.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses the practical content of Islamic law as evidence for Muhammad's prophethood, and how the harmful teachings of false claimants confirm the truth of Islam.

Core Idea
The wisdom and benefit of Islamic law itself is a proof of prophethood.

In this passage, Al-Nasafi explains the second of two proofs for prophethood: the practical evidence. He argues that the very content of Islamic legislation—its acts of worship and sunnahs—demonstrates its divine origin because they align with sound reason and wisdom. He then contrasts this with the harmful commands of false prophets like Mani and Mazdak, whose laws lead to corruption, thereby proving their falsehood.

The Miracle Proof of Prophethood
Al-Nasafi argues that Muhammad's miracles transcend natural and psychic powers, proving their divine origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Nasafi argues that the miracles of Prophet Muhammad are divine proofs, distinct from natural phenomena and human psychic abilities.

Core Idea
Miracles are divine proofs because they transcend both natural laws and human psychic powers.

Al-Nasafi presents the second proof of prophethood: the miracles brought by the Prophet. He argues that these miracles are not merely extraordinary; they are beyond the reach of natural causation and human manipulation. This establishes their divine origin as confirmations of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and proof
Read the passage to understand that the Prophet's proof matches his claim of a divine mission. The miracles are presented as the evidence.
2
Examine the two alternatives
Notice how al-Nasafi first argues that miracles cannot come from natural powers, then from psychic powers. Understand the distinction.
Miracles are not just extraordinary; they are beyond all human capacity.
3
Reflect on the examples
Consider the specific miracles listed (reviving sheep, speaking camel, etc.) and why experts in natural principles confirm their impossibility under natural laws.
These examples are chosen to show the supernatural nature of the miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ ثانيًا : بينة الرسول مطابقة لدعواه]
فأما بينته فمطابقة لدعواه أنه ادعى أمرًا إلهيًا وأتى بالبينات الإلهية التي تفوق قوى الخلق، ولن يأتى حصولها بالقوى الطبيعية - فإن المحققين في معرفة الأصول الطبيعية العارفين بما يجوز أن يترتب تحتها وما لا يجوز متيقنون أن إحياء الشاة المصليَّة وإنطاق الناقة وإلجاء الأسطوانة إلى الحنين، ونبع الماء من بين الأصابع، مما لا يجوز ترتبها تحت أسرار الطبائع ، وكذا شق القمر وغيره على ما نبين إذا انتهينا إلى إقامة الدليل على ذلك إن شاء الله تعالى - ولا بالقوى النفسانية إذ الملتحق بالتدابير النفسانية إما أن يترتب تحت السحر والعزائم أو تحت اللطف والشعبذة، والعالمون بهذه الأمور يعرفون أن ما أتى به من المعجزات خارج عن هذه الوجوه، ونكشف عن ذلك أيضا بعد هذا ذلك أيضًا بعد هذا - إن شاء الله تعالى.
[Second: The proof of the messenger matches his claim]
As for his proof, it matches his claim: he claimed a divine matter and brought divine proofs that surpass the powers of creation, and cannot be obtained by natural powers - for the verifiers in knowledge of natural principles, who know what can and cannot be subsumed under them, are certain that reviving the roasted sheep, giving speech to the she-camel, making the column yearn, and the gushing of water from between the fingers cannot possibly be subsumed under the secrets of natures; likewise the splitting of the moon and others, as we will explain when we come to establishing the proof of that, God willing - nor by psychic powers, for what is connected to psychic manipulations is either subsumed under sorcery and incantations or under subtlety and sleight of hand; and those knowledgeable in these matters know that what he brought of miracles is outside these categories. And we will uncover that also after this, that also after this, God willing.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage presents the second (in sequence) proof: the miracles of the messenger. Al-Nasafi states that Muhammad claimed a divine mission and brought divine proofs that exceed human capacities. He then argues that these miracles cannot be produced by natural forces, as experts in natural principles confirm that specific miracles (reviving a roasted sheep, making a camel speak, causing a pillar to yearn, water flowing from fingers, splitting the moon) are impossible under natural causation. Nor can they be attributed to psychic powers such as sorcery, incantations, or sleight of hand, as knowledgeable people recognize these miracles do not fall under those categories. The miracles are therefore unique divine confirmations of his prophethood.

Misconception: Miracles are just rare natural events or advanced human tricks.
Correction: Miracles are divinely granted events that go beyond both natural laws and any human psychic or technical capability.

Key Takeaway

The Absence of Motives for Rejection
Al-Nasafi argues that no valid grounds exist to reject Muhammad's prophethood because his character is free from four defects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses the absence of four specific defects to prove the credibility of the Prophet's claim.

Core Idea
A prophet's character must be free from four defects for his claim to be valid.

Al-Nasafi presents the third proof for the prophethood of Muhammad: the absence of any motive for rejection. He explains that Muhammad's state is free from four flaws that would invalidate his claim. This passage establishes a key criterion for verifying prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the four defects listed.
The passage is part of a larger argument about proofs of prophethood.
2
Identify the four defects
Find the four meanings (معاني) mentioned: كفر, كذب, فسق, جهل. Understand each term and why it would disqualify a claimant.
These are specific to the claim of prophethood, not general sins.
3
Connect to the overall argument
Reflect on how the absence of these defects supports the claim. Since none are found, the claim stands unchallenged.
This is the third proof in Al-Nasafi's sequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ثالثًا دواعي الجرح منتفية عن بينة الرسول]:
وأما دواعي الجرح فمنتفية عن دعواه، ومعرفة ذلك بوجود أحواله كلها سالمة عن المعاني الأربعة : أحدها الكفر بالله تعالى والثاني الكذب على الله تعالى. والثالث الفسق في أوامر الله تعالى والرابع الجهل بأحكام الله تعالى. وشيء من هذه لم يثبت في حقه.

As for the motives for rejection, they are absent from his claim. And knowledge of that is by all his states being free of the four meanings: first, disbelief in God Almighty; second, lying against God Almighty; third, disobedience in God's commands; fourth, ignorance of God's rulings. None of these has been established against him.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof: the absence of any motive to reject the messenger. Al-Nasafi argues that there are no valid grounds to reject Muhammad's claim because his entire state is free from four defects: disbelief (kufr), lying (kadhib), disobedience (fisq), and ignorance (jahl). Since none of these are found in him, his claim stands unchallenged.

Key Terms

Correction: The text only states freedom from these four specific defects (kufr, kadhib, fisq, jahl) that would invalidate his claim. It does not claim absolute sinlessness in all matters.

The Absence of Motives for Discrediting the Prophet's Claim
Nasafi lists four vices absent from the Prophet's character.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the absence of four vices in the Prophet's character removes all motives for rejecting his prophetic claim.

Core Idea
The Prophet's freedom from four vices proves his claim is genuine.

Nasafi presents a logical argument: if the Prophet had any motive to lie or was characterized by disbelief, sinfulness, or ignorance, his claim could be doubted. But his entire state was free from these four vices. This lesson examines those four qualities and how their absence confirms his truthfulness.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the four qualities listed.
The passage is concise; each quality is a distinct point.
2
Identify the four vices
Identify the Arabic terms for the four vices: kufr, kadhib, fisq, jahl. Understand what each means in this context.
These are not minor faults but fundamental vices that would discredit a prophet.
3
Understand why each vice is a motive
For each vice, ask: why would the presence of this vice give people a reason to discredit the Prophet's claim? For example, disbelief would show he lacks faith in the One he claims to represent.
The absence of all four means there is no ground for rejection.
4
Reflect on the argument's strength
Consider how this argument complements the earlier one (positive signs). Together they form a comprehensive proof of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما دواعي الجرح فمنتفية عن دعواه، ومعرفة ذلك بوجود أحواله كلها سالمة عن المعاني الأربعة: أحدها الكفر بالله تعالى والثاني الكذب على الله تعالى. والثالث الفسق في أوامر الله تعالى والرابع الجهل بأحكام الله تعالى. وشيء من هذه لم يثبت في حقه.

Knowledge of that is by all his states being free of four meanings: first, disbelief in Allah Almighty; second, lying about Allah Almighty; third, disobedience in the commands of Allah Almighty; fourth, ignorance of the rulings of Allah Almighty. None of these is established in his regard.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage presents the second argument for the authenticity of the Prophet’s claim: the complete absence of any motive that would discredit him (dawa'i al-jarh). The author explains that this is known by observing that the Prophet’s entire conduct was free from four negative qualities: disbelief (kufr), lying about Allah (kadhb 'ala Allah), sinfulness (fisq) in carrying out God’s commands, and ignorance (jahl) of God’s rulings. Since none of these was ever proven about him, there is no reason to doubt his truthfulness.

Safety of the Prophet's Claim from Contradiction
Nasafi explains two aspects of the claim's consistency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two aspects of how the Prophet's claim to prophethood is protected from internal contradiction: the safety of the proof through challenge, and the safety of the claim through consistency with rational evidence.

Core Idea
The Prophet's claim is consistent because he challenged all and no one responded, and he affirmed only reason-proven prophets.

This passage from Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla presents the fourth proof of prophethood: the safety of the Prophet's claim from contradiction. The author explains that this safety manifests in two ways. First, the proof itself (the miracle) was presented as a challenge, and no one could refute it. Second, the content of the claim — that he is a prophet — is consistent because he accepts only those whom reason proves to be true prophets and rejects all false claimants. This lesson unpacks both aspects.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of safety from contradiction
Read the passage orientation. The Prophet's claim is safe when it cannot be logically contradicted from any angle.
This is part of a larger argument for prophethood.
2
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the two 'amma... fa...' structures that introduce the two aspects.
3
First aspect: Safety of the proof
Identify the argument: the Prophet challenged everyone to produce something like his miracle, gave them time, and no one attempted. This shows the proof is uncontested.
Nasafi says it is so obvious he won't elaborate.
4
Second aspect: Safety of the claim
Focus on the consistency: the Prophet confirmed prophets whom reason proves true (like Noah, Abraham, Moses) and rejected those whom reason proves false (like Mani, Marqion, Daysan). This shows his claim is not arbitrary.
The example of rejecting dualists (Mani, etc.) is supported by Quranic verse.
5
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how these two aspects together protect the Prophet's claim from any logical contradiction. What would it mean if he had denied a true prophet or confirmed a false one?
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما سلامة البيئة عن مناقضة ترد عليها فمتعلقة بأن يتحدى جميع طبقات المبعوث إليهم على إيراد مثلها ويمهلهم ويقرعهم بالعجز عنه ثم لا يوجد في جماعتهم من يشتغل بمعارضته بذلك، وثبوت هذا الأمر فى حقه عليه السلام أظهر من أن نشتغل ببيانه. على أنا نبين ذلك بعد هذا - إن شاء الله تعالى. وأما سلامة دعواه عن المناقضة فمتعلقة بتصديقه بنبوة من شهد العقل على أنه نبي وتكذيبه من شهد العقل أنه ليس بنبي طلبًا لمقارنة أتباعه، وعن تكذيب من شهد العقل أنه نبي قصدًا لتشيين أمر من ناواه من أشياعه، وكانت دعواه عن الله سالمة عن هذين الأمرين إذ هو عليه السلام صدق من قبله ممن قامت الدلالة على نبوته بعد ثبوت إمكان دعوته كنوح وإبراهيم وموسى وغيره من الأنبياء والرسل عليهم السلام، وكذب جميع من قامت الدلالة على كونه كاذبًا في دعواه النبوة فإنه عليه السلام كذب ماني ومرقيون وديصان لما وجد في كتابه المنزل عليه قوله تعالى: (الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ الَّذِى خَلَقَ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ وَجَعَلَ الظُّلُمَتِ وَالنُّورَ) أخبر أنهما مجعولان مخلوقان وليسا بقديمين خلافا لما يقوله جميع طبقات التنويه، وكذب
As for the safety of the proof from a contradiction that could be brought against it, it is connected to him challenging all classes of those to whom he was sent to produce something like it, and giving them respite, and declaring them incapable of it, and then no one among their company busies themselves with opposing it in that way. The establishment of this matter in his regard, peace be upon him, is more evident than that we should occupy ourselves with explaining it; indeed, we will show that after this, God willing. As for the safety of his claim from contradiction, it is connected to his confirming the prophethood of one whom reason bears witness that he is a prophet, and his disbelieving him whom reason bears witness that he is not a prophet, seeking to attract his followers, and [it is also connected to] not rejecting one whom reason bears witness that he is a prophet, intent on giving strength to the matter of one who opposes him among his partisans. And his claim from Allah was safe from these two matters, for he, peace be upon him, confirmed those before him for whom the evidence of their prophethood was established after the establishment of the possibility of their call, like Noah, Abraham, Moses and other prophets and messengers, peace be upon them; and he rejected all for whom the evidence was established that they were false in their claim to prophethood. Indeed, he rejected Mani, Marqion, and Daysan because he found in his revealed book His saying, 'Praise be to Allah who created the heavens and the earth and made the darkness and the light'; He informed that they are both made and created, not eternal, contrary to what all classes of the dualists say. And he rejected...
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage discusses the fourth argument for the Prophet's authenticity: the safety of his claim from contradiction (salamat al-da'wa 'an al-munaqada). This is presented in two parts. First, the safety of the proof (bayyina) itself: the Prophet challenged all classes of people to produce something like his miracle, gave them time, declared their inability, and no one ever attempted a response. The author notes that this is so obvious it needs no elaboration. Second, the safety of the claim itself: the Prophet consistently affirmed those prophets whom reason proves to be genuine (e.g., Noah, Abraham, Moses) and rejected those whom reason proves false (e.g., Mani, Marqion, Daysan). He never denied a true prophet to attract followers, nor confirmed a false prophet to undermine opponents. His rejection of the dualists is supported by the Quranic verse (al-An'am 6:1) affirming the creation of darkness and light, contradicting their belief in two eternal principles. The text ends mid-sentence, likely continuing with further examples of false claimants.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the Prophet accepted previous prophets only for political reasons or tribal affiliation.
Correction: Nasafi shows that the Prophet's confirmation was based on rational evidence (shahida al-‘aql) of their prophethood, not personal bias. He rejected false claimants like Mani even though they had followers.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is one way the Prophet's claim is safe from contradiction?
A) He performed many miracles.
B) He confirmed only those prophets whom reason proves true and rejected those whom reason proves false.
C) He never claimed prophethood in the first place.
D) He only spoke about himself.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's claim to prophethood is invulnerable to internal contradiction because his proof was unchallenged and his affirmation of other prophets was rationally consistent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you affirm a belief, do you test it for internal consistency as the Prophet's claim was tested? Where in your life do you hold contradictory beliefs that you have not examined?
?
The Prophet's affirmation of previous prophets was based on rational evidence. Are your own affirmations of religious truths grounded in reason or mere tradition? What would it take for you to apply the same standard of rational consistency to your own convictions?
?
The Prophet rejected false claimants like Mani and Marqion despite any potential social or political cost. In your life, do you have the courage to reject falsehood even when it is popular or convenient? What falsehood have you been tolerating that you need to decisively reject?

The Fourth Condition: Claim Free from Contradiction
Discussion of the fourth condition: the prophet's claim must be immune to contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth condition for verifying a prophetic claim: the claim must be free from contradiction, and its two aspects of environmental safety and doctrinal consistency.

Core Idea
A prophetic claim is verified by its consistency with truth and immunity from contradiction.

Imam Nasafi now presents the fourth condition: the prophet's claim must be free from contradiction. This condition ensures that the claim aligns with reason and previous revelations. The passage explains two dimensions: the safety of the environment (no effective opposition) and the safety of the claim itself (affirming true prophets and denying false ones).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aspects of safety
Read the passage and locate where the author divides safety into 'safety of the environment' and 'safety of the claim'. Notice the Arabic terms 'salama al-bi'a' and 'salama al-da'wa'.
The author states this division explicitly.
2
Examine the examples of affirmation and denial
The author lists prophets affirmed (Noah, Abraham, Moses) and false claimants denied (Mani, Marcion, Daysan, Mazdak, Zoroaster). Reflect on why these examples are chosen.
The denials are based on Quranic verses and hadith.
3
Understand the role of the listener's knowledge
The passage explains how a fair-minded listener, knowing the prophet's background and the perfection of the claim, becomes certain. Consider how this strengthens the argument.
The prophet's illiteracy and the ignorance of his people are highlighted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعًا دعوى الرسول سالمة عن المناقضة]: وأما سلامة البيئة عن مناقضة ترد عليها فمتعلقة بأن يتحدى جميع طبقات المبعوث إليهم على إيراد مثلها ويمهلهم ويقرعهم بالعجز عنه ثم لا يوجد في جماعتهم من يشتغل بمعارضته بذلك ، وثبوت هذا الأمر فى حقه عليه السلام أظهر من أن نشتغل ببيانه. على أنا نبين ذلك بعد هذا - إن شاء الله تعالى. وأما سلامة دعواه عن المناقضة فمتعلقة بتصديقه بنبوة من شهد العقل على أنه نبي وتكذيبه من شهد العقل أنه ليس بنبي طلبًا لمقارنة أتباعه، وعن تكذيب من شهد العقل أنه نبي قصدًا لتشيين أمر من ناواه من أشياعه، وكانت دعواه عن الله سالمة عن هذين الأمرين إذ هو عليه السلام صدق من قبله ممن قامت الدلالة على نبوته بعد ثبوت إمكان دعوته كنوح وإبراهيم وموسى وغيره من الأنبياء والرسل عليهم السلام، وكذب جميع من قامت الدلالة على كونه كاذبًا في دعواه النبوة فإنه عليه السلام كذب ماني ومرقيون وديصان لما وجد في كتابه المنزل عليه قوله تعالى: (الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ الَّذِى خَلَقَ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ وَجَعَلَ الظُّلُمَتِ وَالنُّورَ ) أخبر أنهما مجعولان مخلوقان وليسا بقديمين خلافا لما يقوله جميع طبقات التنويه، وكذب مزدك وزرادشت بقوله: القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة، وبما أتى به من التوحيد ونفي الشرك الله تعالى وبالوقوف على هذه المقدمة يعلم أن لا سبيل إلى رد دعواه بل يغلب على قلب كل منصف الميلان إلى قبوله، ثم إذا انضم إلى ذلك علم السامع بحالته من نشوئه بين ظهراني قوم لم يكن لهم علم بما سبق من الأنبياء ولا بشرائعهم ولا العلم بالتوحيد وصفات الصانع القديم ولا معرفة صيانة الدعوى عما يناقض هذه المعاني الأربعة التي بينا، ولا العلم بقوانين العلوم النظرية ثم رأى بأنه أتى بهذه الدعوى المنزهة عن التناقض وتمكن أضداد هذه المعاني الأربعة تيقن بصدقه في دعواه ولم يتخالجه ريب في صحة ما ادعاه، والله الموفق.
Fourth: The claim of the messenger is free from contradiction. As for the safety of the environment from an effective contradiction, it pertains to his challenging all classes of those sent to, to produce something like it, and giving them respite, and striking them with incapability of it, then there is not found among their group anyone who occupies himself with opposing him by that. And the establishment of this matter in his right, peace be upon him, is more evident than that we occupy ourselves with explaining it. However, we will explain that after this, if Allah wills. And as for the safety of his claim from contradiction, it pertains to his affirming the prophethood of one whom reason testifies is a prophet, and his denying the prophethood of one whom reason testifies is not a prophet, in seeking the adhesion of his followers; and his abstaining from denying one whom reason testifies is a prophet, intentionally seeking to weaken the matter of one who opposes him from his partisans. And his claim from Allah was free from these two matters, for he, peace be upon him, affirmed those before him from whom the evidence for their prophethood stood after the establishment of the possibility of their call, like Noah, Abraham, Moses, and other prophets and messengers, peace be upon them; and he denied all those for whom the evidence stood for their being false in their claim to prophethood, for he, peace be upon him, denied Mani, Marcion, and Daysan, because he found in his revealed book the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'Praise be to Allah who created the heavens and the earth and made the darkness and the light' – He informed that both are created and made, not eternal, contrary to what all classes of the dualists say; and he denied Mazdak and Zoroaster by his saying: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation', and by what he brought of tawhid and negation of shirk from Allah the Exalted. And by pausing upon this introduction, it is known that there is no way to reject his claim, but rather the inclination towards accepting it overcomes the heart of every fair person. Then when there is added to that the listener's knowledge of his state, his upbringing among a people who had no knowledge of the previous prophets nor of their laws, nor knowledge of tawhid and the attributes of the eternal Maker, nor knowledge of safeguarding the claim from what contradicts these four meanings which we have explained, nor knowledge of the principles of theoretical sciences; then he saw that he brought this claim free from contradiction and the opposites of these four meanings were firmly established – he becomes certain of his truthfulness in his claim, and no doubt enters his mind regarding the correctness of what he claimed. And Allah is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth condition for verifying a prophetic claim: the claim must be free from contradiction (salama 'an al-munaqada). The author divides it into two aspects. First, the safety of the environment (salama al-bi'a): the prophet challenges all people to produce something similar, gives them time, and declares their inability; no one among them effectively opposes him. The author notes that this is obvious for Prophet Muhammad. Second, the safety of the claim itself: the prophet must not affirm a false prophet nor deny a true one for partisan reasons. The author applies this to Prophet Muhammad: he affirmed previous true prophets (Noah, Abraham, Moses) and denied false claimants (Mani, Marcion, Daysan, Mazdak, Zoroaster). He also brought tawhid and negation of shirk. The author then describes how a fair-minded listener, knowing the prophet's background (unlettered, among a people ignorant of previous revelations and theology), and seeing the claim's perfection, becomes certain of his truthfulness.

السلامة البيئة

تكذيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the absence of contradiction alone suffices, but the author also emphasizes the prophet's background and the audience's knowledge.
Correction: The passage shows that environmental safety (no effective opposition) and the prophet's personal history (unlettered, among ignorant people) are also crucial for certainty.

Checkpoint
What are the two aspects of the safety (salama) of the prophet's claim from contradiction according to the author?
A) Safety of the environment and safety of the claim itself
B) Safety of the prophet's lineage and safety of his message
C) Safety from miracles and safety from reason
D) Safety from opposition and safety from doubt

Key Takeaway
The fourth condition ensures the prophet's claim is consistent with reason and previous revelations, confirming his truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does the prophet's affirmation of previous true prophets challenge your own attitude towards earlier revelations? Do you truly respect all prophets, or do you harbor biases that contradict the consistency of the prophetic message?
?
When you hear a claim about religion, do you check its consistency with reason and past revelation, or do you accept it blindly? What would it mean for you to be as fair-minded as the listener described in this passage?
?
If you were born among people ignorant of previous revelations, as the Prophet was, would you still be able to recognize truth when it comes? What steps can you take to cultivate that discernment and certainty in your own heart?

Proof of Muhammad's Prophethood by Analogy
Analogical proof: Muhammad's prophethood is proven like that of Moses and Jesus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) is proven through an analogy with the prophethood of Moses and Jesus, based on shared evidence of miracles and reliable transmission.

Core Idea
Prophethood is proven by miracles and trustworthy transmission; the same evidence applies to all prophets.

This lesson introduces a powerful rational argument from analogy. The author first lays down a logical principle: if two cases share the same type of evidence and cause, they share the same conclusion. He then applies this to prophethood: the message of Moses was established by miracles witnessed and reliably transmitted, and the same applies to Jesus. The implication is clear: Muhammad's prophethood is proven by the same kind of evidence. This concise proof forms the backbone of the rational defense of prophethood in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the concise and logical style of the author.
2
Identify the general principle
Find the sentence that states the logical rule: whoever shares the same evidence and cause shares the same result. Understand why this is foundational.
This principle is known as qiyas (analogical reasoning).
3
Apply to Moses and Jesus
See how the author applies the principle to Moses: his prophethood was proven by miracles (breaking customs) witnessed and transmitted by a group for whom collusion is impossible. Then note the same applies to Jesus.
The transmission method (tawatur) is key to establishing historical reliability.
4
Reflect on Muhammad
Consider how this same evidence—miracles and reliable transmission—applies to Muhammad. Think about the Quran as a miracle and its preservation.
The author implies but does not explicitly state the conclusion here.
5
Understand the role of tawatur
Discuss why the impossibility of collusion (tawatur) is crucial for establishing the truth of prophetic miracles.
This prevents the accusation of fabrication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التدليل على ثبوت رسالة سيدنا محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام] وبعد الوقوف على هذه المقدمة نقول : لا شك أن من ساوى غيره في الدليل والعلة ساواه في المدلول والمعلول. ثم إن موسى عليه السلام ثبتت رسالته لقيام الدلالة على ثبوتها وهي المعجزات الناقضات للعادات على يديه عاينها من شهدها وبلغ من لم يشاهدها على ألسنة قوم لم يجز عليهم التواطؤ في العادات الجارية، فصار ذلك كالمعاين المشاهد لهم. وكذلك رسالة عيسى عليه السلام ثبتت أيضًا بهذا الطريق.
The proof of the establishment of the message of our master Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him). After pausing upon this introduction, we say: There is no doubt that whoever equals another in the evidence and the cause equals him in the evidenced effect and the effect. Then, Moses (peace be upon him) his message was established due to the evidence for its establishment, which are miracles breaking the customs at his hands, witnessed by those who saw them, and conveyed to those who did not witness them through the tongues of a people for whom collusion in the usual customs is not permissible, so that became like being seen and witnessed for them. Likewise, the message of Jesus (peace be upon him) was also established by this path.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage presents an analogical argument (qiyas). The author first states a general principle: if two things share the same evidence (dalil) and cause ('illa), they share the same result (madlul and ma'lul). He then applies it: the prophethood of Moses was proven by miracles that break customs, witnessed by contemporaries and reliably transmitted by a group for whom collusion is impossible. The same applies to Jesus. The implication is that Muhammad's prophethood is proven by the same type of evidence (miracles and reliable transmission). This is a concise rational proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think this argument requires the miracles of Muhammad to be identical in form to those of Moses and Jesus.
Correction: The author does not require identical miracles; rather, the shared type of evidence (miracles breaking customs and reliable transmission) is sufficient to apply the analogy.

Checkpoint
According to the author, how is the prophethood of Moses and Jesus established?
A) Through rational argument alone
B) Through miracles witnessed and reliably transmitted by a trustworthy group
C) Through philosophical proofs
D) Through scripture alone

Key Takeaway
The prophethood of Muhammad is proven by the same kind of miracles and reliable transmission that established the prophethood of Moses and Jesus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you had been born at the time of the Prophet and witnessed his miracles with your own eyes, would your faith be stronger or weaker than it is now? Why? And what does your answer reveal about your reliance on the tawatur that the passage describes as 'like being seen and witnessed'?
?
The passage argues that the same evidence applies to all prophets. Do you treat the Prophet Muhammad's message with the same urgency and obedience as if he were standing before you right now? Which specific command of his do you most resist obeying, and what will you do about it today?
?
Many people claim to believe in the prophethood of Muhammad but live as if it doesn't affect their daily choices. In what area of your life—your speech, your business dealings, your relationships—does your behavior most contradict your claim of belief? What is one concrete change you will make this week to align your actions with that belief?

Conditions for Accepting a Prophetic Claim
The author explains how a prophetic claim becomes undeniable when certain conditions are met.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a prophetic claim becomes undeniable when certain conditions are met, including the claimant's message of tawhid and the listener's knowledge of the claimant's background.

Core Idea
A prophetic claim gains certainty when it brings tawhid and arises from an ignorant community.

This passage from Imam Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla discusses the epistemological grounds for accepting a prophetic claim. The author argues that when a person claims prophethood and brings monotheism, and when the listener knows that the claimant grew up among people ignorant of divine knowledge, the claim becomes undeniable. This lesson explores these conditions and their cumulative effect on certainty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the translation. Notice the logical flow from the initial premise to the conclusion.
The passage opens with a quote attributed to Zoroaster.
2
Identify the key conditions
Find the conditions that make the claim undeniable: the message of tawhid, the listener's knowledge of the claimant's ignorant background, and the claim's freedom from contradiction.
3
Understand the role of the four meanings
The passage mentions 'these four meanings' previously explained. Consider how these meanings relate to the claimant's integrity.
The four meanings are not defined here but are part of the broader argument.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that with these conditions, the listener becomes certain and no doubt remains. Ask yourself why this reasoning is persuasive.
Note that the background ignorance of the community reinforces the miraculous nature of the claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزرادشت بقوله: القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة (٢)، وبما أتى به من التوحيد ونفي الشرك الله تعالى وبالوقوف على هذه المقدمة يعلم أن لا سبيل إلى رد دعواه بل يغلب على قلب كل منصف الميلان إلى قبوله، ثم إذا انضم إلى ذلك علم السامع بحالته من نشوئه بين ظهراني قوم لم يكن لهم علم بما سبق من الأنبياء ولا بشرائعهم ولا العلم بالتوحيد وصفات الصانع القديم ولا (٣) معرفة صيانة الدعوى عما يناقض هذه المعاني الأربعة التي بينا، ولا العلم بقوانين العلوم النظرية ثم رأى بأنه أتى بهذه الدعوى المنزهة عن التناقض وتمكن أضداد هذه المعاني الأربعة تيقن بصدقه في دعواه ولم يتخالجه ريب في صحة ما ادعاه (٤)، والله الموفق.
And Zoroaster said: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this ummah' (2), and with what he brought of tawhid and negation of shirk from Allah Most High, and by understanding this premise, one knows that there is no way to reject his claim, rather the inclination to accept it overcomes the heart of every fair person. Then when there is added to that the listener's knowledge of his condition, that he grew up among a people who had no knowledge of what came before from the prophets nor of their laws, nor knowledge of tawhid and the attributes of the Eternal Maker, nor (3) knowledge of safeguarding the claim from what contradicts these four meanings which we have explained, nor knowledge of the laws of theoretical sciences, and then he sees that he came with this claim purified from contradiction, and the opposites of these four meanings are possible, he becomes certain of his truthfulness and no doubt enters his heart about the correctness of what he claimed (4). And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a preliminary discussion of the epistemological certainty that arises when a prophetic claim meets certain conditions. The author begins by quoting a statement attributed to Zoroaster (or citing a hadith) and then focuses on the claimant who brings monotheism and negation of shirk. The key point is that once the listener understands the premise (المقدمة) that such a claim cannot be rejected, the heart of a fair person inclines towards acceptance. The author then lists additional factors that reinforce certainty: the claimant's upbringing among a people ignorant of previous prophets, scriptures, tawhid, divine attributes, and theoretical sciences; and the claimant's ability to present a claim free from contradiction, while the opposites of the four previously explained meanings remain possible. This combination leaves no room for doubt. The passage underscores that the background ignorance of the community actually strengthens the miraculous nature of the claim.

صانع قديم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A prophet's claim is weakened if his people are ignorant.
Correction: The author shows that ignorance of the community reinforces the claim's miraculous and undeniable nature, because the claimant could not have acquired such knowledge from his environment.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does the listener's knowledge of the claimant's background contribute to the acceptance of his claim?
A) It creates doubt about the claim.
B) It increases certainty when combined with the claim's purity from contradiction.
C) It is irrelevant to the assessment.
D) It proves the claimant is lying.

Key Takeaway
A prophetic claim becomes undeniable when it is based on tawhid, arises from an ignorant community, and is free from contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a message that calls to pure tawhid, do you examine it fairly, or do you let your assumptions about the messenger's background (e.g., education, social status) cloud your judgment? This lesson demands that the very ignorance of the messenger can be a sign of truth. Where in your life have you dismissed a truth because of its source?
?
Have you ever rejected a truth because it seemed too simple or came from an unexpected place, only to later realize its coherence and power? This lesson says a claim free from contradiction, arising from ignorance, should compel acceptance. What truth have you been avoiding that meets these criteria?
?
The passage describes a 'fair person' whose heart inclines to accept truth when it is undeniable. Are you such a person? What would it take for you to move from inclination to certainty in the matters of faith? Be specific: which condition from this lesson do you need to see fulfilled in your own life?

Prophethood
beginner
5 min
The Universal Principle of Analogy in Prophethood Proofs
The author states a universal principle and applies it to Moses and Jesus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a universal logical principle about equality in evidence and cause is used to establish that the proofs for Muhammad's prophethood are identical in kind to those of Moses and Jesus.

Core Idea
Equality in evidence means equality in what is evidenced.

This passage introduces a key logical move: the author first states a universal principle about evidence and causation, then applies it to the cases of Moses and Jesus to prepare the ground for Muhammad. The principle is simple but powerful: if two things are equal in their evidence, they are equal in what that evidence proves.

Guided Path
1
Understand the universal principle
Read the first sentence carefully: whoever equals another in evidence and cause equals him in the evidenced and caused. This is the logical foundation.
This is a general rule about any two things being compared.
2
Apply to Moses
See how Moses' prophethood was proven by miracles witnessed or reliably transmitted, and that transmission is considered like direct observation.
The concept of 'tawatur' (multiple independent chains) ensures reliability.
3
Apply to Jesus
Note that the same method applies to Jesus, establishing a pattern for all prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و[التدليل على ثبوت رسالة سيدنا محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام] وبعد الوقوف على هذه المقدمة نقول : لا شك أن من ساوى غيره في الدليل والعلة ساواه في المدلول والمعلول. ثم إن موسى عليه السلام ثبتت رسالته لقيام الدلالة على ثبوتها وهي المعجزات الناقضات للعادات على يديه عاينها من شهدها وبلغ من لم يشاهدها على ألسنة قوم لم يجز عليهم التواطؤ في العادات الجارية، فصار ذلك كالمعاين (٥) المشاهد لهم. وكذلك رسالة عيسى عليه السلام ثبتت أيضًا بهذا الطريق. ثم من المعارف الأولية التى لا يداخلها شك ولا يخالطها ريبة ولا شبهة، أن الاستواء في الأدلة يطلب من حيث المعنى الذي به صارت الأدلة أدلة له من حيث الصور التي لم تكن الأدلة أدلة (١) لأجلها ، ثم قلب العصا حية (٢) وتفجير الماء من الصخرة الصماء (٣) وإحياء الموتى، وإبراء الأكمة والأبرص (٤) ، وغير ذلك مما كانت دلائل وحججًا لصحة الرسالة لا لصورها بل لخروجها عن العادات، وامتناع دخولها تحت القدرة المحدثة، واختصاصها بدخولها تحت قدرة الصانع الحكيم الذي لا يعجزه شيء، ولا يقيم الدلالة على صحة الفاسد وصدق الكاذب وثبوتها عقيب دعوى الرسالة. أنه (٥) ثم إن رسولنا المصطفى محمد ساوى غيره من الأنبياء فيما هو دلالة النبوة والرسالة وفيما هو من خواص النبوة، فيساويهم في صحة دعواه ووجوب قبول ما ادعى أنه (٩) من عند الله، وتصديقه في جميع ذلك، فمن أقر بنبوة غيره وأنكر نبوته وكذبه في دعواه فقد وقع في ذلك، إما لصد الشيطان إياه عن التأمل في آياته وإما لتمسكه بما ورثه من آبائه تقليدًا لهم، وإما لسلوكه سبيل البغي والحسد واشتغاله بالتعصب لجيل من الأجيال وأمة من الأمم عصمنا الله تعالى عن الوقوع في الضلالة لسلوك سبيل الجهالة. ثم لا وقوف على صحة ما ادعينا من مساواته غيره من الرسل إلا بعد إبانة آياته، وإثبات اختصاصه فيما هو من خواص النبوة، فنبدأ بالإبانة عن آياته فنقول :
And [The proof of establishing the message of our master Muhammad, peace be upon him]. After understanding this premise, we say: There is no doubt that whoever equals another in evidence and cause equals him in the evidenced and the caused. Then Moses, peace be upon him, his message was established due to the existence of the evidence of its establishment, which are the miracles that break customs at his hands; those who witnessed them saw them, and it reached those who did not witness them through the tongues of a people about whom collusion in the usual customs is not considered possible, so that became like the eyewitness (5) who observed them. Likewise, the message of Jesus, peace be upon him, was also established by this method. Then it is among the primary cognitions that no doubt enters, nor uncertainty or suspicion mixes with them, that equality in evidence is sought in terms of the meaning by which the evidences became evidences for him, not in terms of the forms for which the evidences were not evidences (1). Then the turning of the staff into a serpent (2), the gushing of water from the solid rock (3), reviving the dead, and curing the blind and lepers (4), and other things that were proofs and arguments for the correctness of the message – not because of their forms but because of their breaking of customs, and the impossibility of their falling under created power, and their specificity to fall under the power of the Wise Maker whom nothing escapes, and He does not establish evidence for the correctness of the corrupt or the truthfulness of the liar. And its occurrence after the claim of prophethood. That (5). Then our chosen messenger Muhammad equaled other prophets in what is the proof of prophethood and messengerhood and in what are the characteristics of prophethood, so he equals them in the correctness of his claim and the obligation to accept what he claimed to be from Allah, and to affirm him in all of that. Whoever affirms the prophethood of another and denies his prophethood and falsifies his claim has fallen into that, either due to Satan turning him away from contemplating his signs, or due to his clinging to what he inherited from his fathers by imitation, or due to his taking the path of transgression and envy and preoccupation with fanaticism for a generation or a nation. May Allah protect us from falling into misguidance by taking the path of ignorance. Then the correctness of what we claim of his equality with other messengers cannot be established except after clarifying his signs and proving his distinctiveness in what are the characteristics of prophethood. So we begin with the clarification of his signs and we say:
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a logical proof by analogy for the prophethood of Muhammad. It opens with the heading explicitly stating the topic: proving Muhammad's message. The author first lays down a universal principle: equality in evidence (دليل) and cause (علة) implies equality in what is evidenced (مدلول) and caused (معلول). He then applies this to the case of previous prophets: Moses' prophethood was proven by miracle-working events that break customs ('Breaking customs' means supernatural acts impossible for creatures). These miracles were either directly observed or reliably transmitted through a community whose collusion on a lie is impossible. The same method applies to Jesus. The author then asserts a primary cognition (معارف أولية) that equality in evidence is based on the essential meaning of the evidence, not its specific form. Miracles like the staff turning into a serpent or reviving the dead derive their evidential force from breaking customs and being beyond created power, not from their particular appearance. Since Muhammad performed miracles of the same kind (breaking customs), he equals previous prophets in the proof of prophethood. Therefore, his claim is equally valid, and whoever accepts other prophets but rejects him does so out of satanic distraction, blind imitation, or envy. The author concludes that to fully establish this equality, one must enumerate Muhammad's specific miracles, which he will do next.

Key Terms
دليل
علة
مدلول
معلول
معجزة
نبوة
رسالة
تواطؤ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Muhammad's prophethood is proven by a different kind of evidence than previous prophets.
Correction: The author argues that the same logical principle applies: if the evidence (miracles) is of the same kind (breaking customs), then the conclusion (prophethood) is equally valid.

Checkpoint
What is the universal principle stated at the beginning of the passage?
A) Whoever equals another in evidence and cause equals him in the evidenced and caused.
B) Miracles must be witnessed directly to be valid.
C) All prophets are equal in rank.
D) Prophethood is established by consensus.

Key Takeaway
The foundation of the proof is the logical equivalence: same evidence, same conclusion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When doubts about the truth of Islam arise in your mind, do you actively recall the logical principle that equal evidence demands equal acceptance? If not, what concrete step will you take this week to make this principle a reflexive shield against uncertainty?
?
You have seen that tawatur makes transmitted reports as reliable as direct sight. Does your level of certainty in the Quran and hadith reflect this fact, or do you often treat them with less conviction than if you had seen the events yourself? Commit today to treating transmitted knowledge with the same certainty as direct observation.

The Primary Cognition and the Nature of Miracles
The author explains the primary cognition and the evidential nature of miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the evidential value of miracles lies not in their external form but in their essential characteristic of breaking natural customs and being beyond created power.

Core Idea
Miracles prove prophethood because they break customs, not because of their specific form.

This passage moves from the universal principle to a primary cognition about how equality in evidence is determined. The author clarifies that what makes a miracle a proof is not its specific form (like a staff turning into a snake) but its inner quality of breaking natural laws and being beyond the power of any creature. This insight is crucial for understanding why Muhammad's miracles are equally valid.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the primary cognition
Read the sentence about primary cognition carefully. It says equality in evidence is based on the meaning by which the evidence becomes evidence, not its outward form.
This is a foundational epistemological point.
2
Identify the examples of miracles
Look at the list of miracles: staff to serpent, water from rock, reviving the dead, etc. Notice that they are mentioned only as examples.
The author emphasizes that it is not their form but their breaking of customs that matters.
3
Understand why they are proof
The author explains three reasons: they break customs, they are impossible for created power, and they come from the Wise Maker who does not support false claims.
This shows the logical basis for miracle-based proofs.

Muhammad's Equality and Reasons for Rejection
The author concludes Muhammad's equality and lists reasons for rejection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author concludes that Muhammad equals previous prophets in the proof of prophethood, and why some reject him despite this equality.

Core Idea
Muhammad's prophethood is as valid as any prophet's; rejection stems from distraction, imitation, or envy.

This passage applies the previous arguments directly to Muhammad: since his miracles share the same essential quality of breaking customs, he equals all previous prophets in the proof of prophethood. The author then identifies three psychological or spiritual causes for rejecting his message: satanic distraction, blind imitation, and envy. Finally, he declares that to fully establish this equality, one must examine Muhammad's specific miracles.

Guided Path
1
Follow the conclusion from the premise
Read the first sentence: Muhammad equaled other prophets in what is the proof of prophethood, so he equals them in the correctness of his claim.
This is the direct application of the universal principle.
2
Identify the three causes of rejection
Look at the three reasons the author gives for why someone might accept other prophets but reject Muhammad.
These are psychological/spiritual explanations.
3
Understand the transition to Muhammad's signs
The final sentence says that the complete proof requires enumerating Muhammad's specific signs, which will follow.
This sets up the next section.

This passage is a logical proof by analogy for the prophethood of Muhammad. It opens with the heading explicitly stating the topic: proving Muhammad's message. The author first lays down a universal principle: equality in evidence (دليل) and cause (علة) implies equality in what is evidenced (مدلول) and caused (معلول). He then applies this to the case of previous prophets: Moses' prophethood was proven by miracle-working events that break customs ('Breaking customs' means supernatural acts impossible for creatures). These miracles were either directly observed or reliably transmitted through a community whose collusion on a lie is impossible. The same method applies to Jesus. The author then asserts a primary cognition (معارف أولية) that equality in evidence is based on the essential meaning of the evidence, not its specific form. Miracles like the staff turning into a serpent or reviving the dead derive their evidential force from breaking customs and being beyond created power, not from their particular appearance. Since Muhammad performed miracles of the same kind (breaking customs), he equals previous prophets in the proof of prophethood. Therefore, his claim is equally valid, and whoever accepts other prophets but rejects him does so out of satanic distraction, blind imitation, or envy. The author concludes that to fully establish this equality, one must enumerate Muhammad's specific miracles, which he will do next.

Key Terms
نبوة
رسالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that rejecting Muhammad while accepting other prophets is logically consistent.
Correction: The author argues that since the proof (miracles breaking customs) is the same, accepting one and rejecting the other is contradictory and stems from psychological or moral failings.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the logical consequence of the fact that Muhammad's miracles share the same essential quality as those of previous prophets?
A) Muhammad is greater than previous prophets.
B) Muhammad's claim to prophethood is equally valid.
C) Previous prophets are no longer relevant.
D) Miracles are not necessary for prophethood.

Key Takeaway
Since Muhammad's miracles are of the same kind as previous prophets, his prophethood is equally valid; rejection stems from spiritual or moral failings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever rejected a truth because it clashed with what you inherited from your family or community, without truly examining it? What would it cost you to break that imitation?
?
Is there any area of your life where envy or tribal loyalty blinds you to the truth? Be honest: whose success stirs resentment in you, and how does that affect your acceptance of God's signs?
?
What distractions in your daily life—screens, worries, ambitions—keep you from contemplating the signs of Allah that are all around you? What will you remove today to clear your vision?

Miracles as Proofs and Muhammad's Equality
Al-Nasafi explains the principle of miraculous proofs and Muhammad's equality with other prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that miracles prove prophethood due to their supernatural nature and context, and that Prophet Muhammad is equal to previous prophets in the essential proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
Miracles validate prophets by breaking natural law, not by their form.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi’s Tabsirat al-Adilla lays the foundation for understanding how miracles serve as proofs of prophethood. He argues that the evidentiary power of miracles lies not in their outward form but in their departure from the natural order and their occurrence immediately after a prophetic claim. This principle establishes the equality of all prophets, including Muhammad, in the essential proof of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary cognition
Read the opening sentence: 'Then from the primary cognitions...' and note that the author presents this as an indisputable starting point.
Primary cognitions (ma'arif awwaliyya) are self-evident truths.
2
Understand the principle of miracle proofs
The author explains that miracles are proofs because of their meaning (supernaturalness) not their form, citing examples from previous prophets.
Focus on the phrases 'departure from customs' and 'impossible for created power.'
3
Apply the principle to Prophet Muhammad
The author then argues that Muhammad equaled previous prophets in the validity of his claim, and denial stems from satanic influence, imitation, or envy.
This leads to the need to present Muhammad's signs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم من المعارف الأولية التى لا يداخلها شك ولا يخالطها ريبة ولا شبهة، أن الاستواء في الأدلة يطلب من حيث المعنى الذي به صارت الأدلة أدلة له من حيث الصور التي لم تكن الأدلة أدلة لأجلها ، ثم قلب العصا حية وتفجير الماء من الصخرة الصماء وإحياء الموتى، وإبراء الأكمة والأبرص ، وغير ذلك مما كانت دلائل وحججًا لصحة الرسالة لا لصورها بل لخروجها عن العادات، وامتناع دخولها تحت القدرة المحدثة، واختصاصها بدخولها تحت قدرة الصانع الحكيم الذي لا يعجزه شيء، ولا يقيم الدلالة على صحة الفاسد وصدق الكاذب وثبوتها عقيب دعوى الرسالة.
ثم إن رسولنا المصطفى محمد ساوى غيره من الأنبياء فيما هو دلالة النبوة والرسالة وفيما هو من خواص النبوة، فيساويهم في صحة دعواه ووجوب قبول ما ادعى أنه من عند الله، وتصديقه في جميع ذلك، فمن أقر بنبوة غيره وأنكر نبوته وكذبه في دعواه فقد وقع في ذلك، إما لصد الشيطان إياه عن التأمل في آياته وإما لتمسكه بما ورثه من آبائه تقليدًا لهم، وإما لسلوكه سبيل البغي والحسد واشتغاله بالتعصب لجيل من الأجيال وأمة من الأمم عصمنا الله تعالى عن الوقوع في الضلالة لسلوك سبيل الجهالة.
ثم لا وقوف على صحة ما ادعينا من مساواته غيره من الرسل إلا بعد إبانة آياته، وإثبات اختصاصه فيما هو من خواص النبوة، فنبدأ بالإبانة عن آياته فنقول :
Then from the primary cognitions that no doubt enters them, nor suspicion or uncertainty mixes with them, is that equality in proofs is sought from the aspect of the meaning by which proofs became proofs for him, not from the aspect of the forms for which the proofs were not proofs. Then the turning of the staff into a serpent, and the gushing of water from the solid rock, and the reviving of the dead, and the curing of the blind and the leper, and other things that were proofs and evidences for the validity of the message, not for their forms, but for their departure from customs, and the impossibility of their falling under created power, and their being specific to falling under the power of the Wise Maker whom nothing escapes, and [God] does not establish evidence for the validity of the corrupt or the truthfulness of the liar, and their occurrence after the claim of prophethood. Then our chosen Messenger Muhammad equaled other prophets in what is the proof of prophethood and messengership, and in what is from the particularities of prophethood. So he equals them in the validity of his claim and the obligation of accepting what he claimed is from God, and the affirmation of him in all of that. So whoever affirms the prophethood of another and denies his prophethood and calls him a liar in his claim has fallen into that, either because of Satan turning him away from reflection on his signs, or because of his clinging to what he inherited from his fathers out of imitation of them, or because of his following the path of transgression and envy and his occupation with partisanship for a generation of generations or a community of communities. May God Most High protect us from falling into misguidance by following the path of ignorance. Then there is no stopping at the validity of what we have claimed regarding his equality with other messengers except after the manifestation of his signs, and the establishment of his particularity in what is from the particularities of prophethood. So we begin with the manifestation of his signs, saying:
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument establishing the principle by which miracles (mu'jizat) serve as proofs of prophethood. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, begins by stating that it is a primary cognition (ma'rifa awwaliyya) free from doubt that the evidentiary value of miracles lies in their meaning—their supernatural character—not in their external forms. He gives examples from previous prophets: Moses' staff becoming a serpent, water from the rock, Jesus' reviving the dead and healing the blind and leper. These are proofs not because of their specific forms but because they break natural custom (khuruj 'an al-'adat) and are impossible for created power (imtina' dukhuliha tahta al-qudra al-muhdatha), being specific to the power of the Wise Maker. They are also granted immediately following a claim of prophethood, which distinguishes them from mere extraordinary events. Then al-Nasafi applies this to Prophet Muhammad: he is equal to all previous prophets in the essential proof of prophethood. Therefore, anyone who accepts the prophethood of others but denies Muhammad's prophethood does so due to Satanic turning away, blind imitation of ancestors, or envy and partisanship. Finally, the author announces that to establish this equality, he will now present the signs of Muhammad, beginning with a classification.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles prove prophethood because of their impressive form.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that miracles are proofs because they break natural custom and are impossible for created power, not because of their form.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why do miracles prove prophethood?

B) Because they break natural custom and are beyond created power
C) Because they are ancient
D) Because they are witnessed by many

Key Takeaway
Miracles validate prophethood because they break the natural order, occur after a prophetic claim, and are impossible for any created being.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been more impressed by the form of a miracle (like a dramatic healing or a grand sign) than by what it actually proves about God and His messenger? What does this passage say about your tendency, and how will you adjust your focus starting today?
?
The passage warns that following inherited beliefs from your fathers can lead to rejecting the truth. Is there any belief about religion that you hold simply because you were raised with it, without personally verifying its evidence? Will you commit today to examine one such belief against this lesson's criteria?
?
If you truly accept that Muhammad's proofs equal those of the earlier prophets, does your heart submit to him as fully as it does to them? Or is there a hesitation rooted in envy, partisanship, or unchecked pride? Ask yourself honestly, and let the answer drive you to reflection.

Classification of the Prophet's Signs: Sensory and Rational
Divides the Prophet's signs into sensory and rational and defines sensory signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classification of the Prophet Muhammad's signs into sensory and rational categories, and the threefold division of sensory signs.

Core Idea
Proofs of prophethood are either seen by the eyes or grasped by the mind.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi begins by dividing the signs that prove Muhammad's prophethood into two major categories: sensory and rational. He then defines what makes a sign sensory and provides a three-part classification. This foundational classification helps us organize the many miracles of the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the clear structure: a division, a definition, and a subdivision.
The passage is concise; every sentence introduces a new conceptual layer.
2
Identify the two main categories
Find where the author states the first division of signs. What are the two categories? Note that the passage then focuses on one of them (sensory).
The rational category is mentioned but not elaborated here.
3
Analyze the threefold division of sensory signs
After defining sensory signs, the author divides them into three types. List them and think of examples from the Prophet's life for each.
This threefold structure will be used in the following sections to discuss specific miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الآيات الدالة على رسالته حسية وعقلية
آیات رسالته لا تنقسم أولا إلى قسمين حسية وعقلية.
أما الحسية منها : وهي ما يظهره الله تعالى للأعين من العجائب المباينة لمجرى الطبائع والبدائع المفارقة للمعهود من العادة وكان له من ذلك ما لا يحصى كثرة.
وهي أقسام ثلاثة : فمنها ما كان خارج ذاته، ومنها ما كان في ذاته ومنها ما كان في أخلاقه.
The signs indicating his messengership are sensory and rational. His signs of messengership are first divided into two divisions: sensory and rational. As for the sensory ones: they are what God Most High makes appear to the eyes of wonders that are different from the course of natures and extraordinary things that depart from what is customary in habit, and he had of that which cannot be counted in multitude. And they are three divisions: some of them are what was outside his being, some of them are what was in his being, and some of them are what was in his character.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage provides a classification of the proof-signs (ayat) of the Prophet Muhammad. The author states that these signs are first divided into two types: sensory (hissiyya) and rational (aqliyya). He then defines sensory signs: they are wonders that God makes appear to the eyes, which break the normal course of nature (mujra al-taba'i') and depart from customary habit. He notes that the Prophet had such signs in great abundance, beyond counting. Then he subdivides sensory signs into three categories: those outside his own person (kharij dhatihi), those in his person (fi dhatihi), and those in his character (fi akhlaqihi). This threefold division organizes the sensory miracles, and the following passages will detail examples of each category.

Key Terms

الآيات العقلية
الطبائع
العادة
خارج ذاته
في ذاته
في أخلاقه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only physical external events count as sensory miracles.
Correction: Sensory miracles include those in the Prophet's own body and character as well, as stated in the threefold division.

Checkpoint
Into how many divisions are the sensory signs of the Prophet divided?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The signs of prophethood are first classified into sensory and rational, and sensory signs are further divided into three types: outside the Prophet, in his person, and in his character.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that the Prophet's signs include sensory marvels both in his person and his character. Which of these three categories—outside, in person, or in character—do you find yourself most drawn to, and why might that be? This week, consciously reflect on one example from the category you neglect most, and ask yourself: 'How can I let this sign deepen my conviction in his prophethood?'
?
The author groups the Prophet's character as a sensory sign witnessed by the eyes. When you look at your own character, do you see it as something that could point others to truth? What would change if you truly believed that your character is a sign that people perceive? Commit to one specific character trait you need to align with the Prophet's example starting today.
?
This lesson divides proofs into sensory and rational. Honestly, do you rely more on intellectual arguments or on stories of miracles when you think about prophethood? If you lean on one side, what does that reveal about your faith? Ask yourself: 'If I only had the other type of proof, would I still be convinced?' Then take a moment to read the source again and notice how both are given equal weight.
